Null identity analysis of top trending words close to (black, negro) for Black World / Negro Digest

Kushal K Dey

4/12/2018

Introduction

In this script, we look at the top trending words related to black and negro for Black World / Negro Digest magazine and then see what happens to the trend when the black and negro words are combined together. Do we see an identity bias?

library(wordVectors)
library(ggplot2)

Load word2vec models

We load the word2vec model fits.

Null identity models

dir <- "../BL_ND_ID/"
ll <- list.files(dir, pattern = ".bin")
model_list_1 <- list()
for(m in 1:length(ll)){
  model_list_1[[m]] = read.vectors(paste0(dir, ll[m]))
}

Association Trend Plotter

trend_plotter <- function(word_set_1, word_set_2, model_list){
  assoc <- c()
  for(m in 1:length(ll)){
  
  assoc <- c(assoc, 
             cosineSimilarity(model_list[[m]][[word_set_1, average = TRUE]], 
                              model_list[[m]][[word_set_2, average = TRUE]]))
  }
  df <- data.frame("year" =  c(1961:1970, 1970:1976),
                   "score" = assoc)
  p <- qplot(year, score, data = df, xlab = "year", ylab = "association score") +  
            geom_smooth(method = "lm", size = 1.5) +
            ggtitle("trend plot")
  p
}

[Black, Negro] vs opportunities

trend_plotter(c("black", "blacks"), c("opportunities"), model_list_1)

Black vs opportunities

trend_plotter(c("black", "blacks"), c("opportunities"), model_list_2)

Negro vs opportunities

trend_plotter(c("negro", "negros", "negroes"), c("opportunities"), model_list_2)
